 we signed a distribution

 an entity related through common management. The agreement
provides us with the right to sell and distribute Gran Nevada's beverages in the United States with purchase prices at the then

renewals of successive five year terms unless terminated.&nbsp; We initiated sales and distribution operations in March 2014.


 2016
 we entered into a Stock Purchase
and Sale Agreement to acquire all of the issued and outstanding common stock of Energy Sources Distributors
 Inc. (&ldquo;ESD&rdquo;)
from its three founding shareholders. ESD provides wholesale distribution of specialty beverage products from its headquarters
in Gilroy
 California. The total purchase price for the acquisition was $450
000 in cash. We retained one of the selling founders
as General Manager for a term of twelve (12) months pursuant to an employment agreement to manage operations at the ESD facility
in Gilroy
 California. ESD is now a wholly-owned subsidiary &nbsp;of the Company.

long-term relationships with our consumers by offering superior
 high quality products at the most competitive prices.






    
    



in our market compete for brand recognition

consumer confidence and are able to readily secure shelf space and media attention for their products.&nbsp;Many of our competitors
also have existing relationships with the same distribution channels and retailers through which we sell our products.&nbsp;We
intend to compete in the market by offering consumers affordable products that taste better and possess a longer shelf life than
most products in the market.

 2017
HISP has initiated a lawsuit against TCA Global Credit Master Fund
 LP (&ldquo;TCA&rdquo;). In the lawsuit
 HISP has asserted five
claims against TCA: (i) declaratory judgment (for application of Florida law
 as opposed to Nevada law); (ii) usury; (iii) violation
of the Florida Deceptive and Unfair Trade Practices Act; (iv) breach of contract; and (v) breach of the implied covenant of good
faith and fair dealing. Specifically
 HISP seeks a declaratory judgment against TCA finding (i) the Nevada choice-of-law clause
in the loan documents is invalid and unenforceable; (ii) Florida law applies and governs the loan documents; (iii) the loan documents
are illegal
 unconscionable
 unenforceable
 and usurious; (iv) any debt owed and stock issued pursuant to the loan documents should
be cancelled and forfeited by TCA
 and thus TCA is estopped from collecting such debt and stock; (v) monetary damages should be
awarded in an amount according to proof; and (vi) reasonable attorneys&rsquo; fees and costs should be awarded.


 not knowing HISP had sued it on June
14
 2017
 sued HISP the next day on June 15
 2017. In the lawsuit filed by TCA
 TCA has asserted four claims against HISP: (i)
amount due on the subject debenture; (ii) amount due on the subject guaranty (only against guarantor Energy Source Distributors
Inc. (&ldquo;ESD&rdquo;)); (iii) foreclosure on security; and (iv) breach of the subject securities purchase agreement. TCA seeks
monetary damages of $952
323
 plus default interest of 25%
 attorneys&rsquo; fees and costs
 and to foreclose on its purported
first-priority

 the guarantor).

with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States). Those standards require that we plan and

taxes. Under the accrual method
 deferred tax assets and liabilities are determined based on the differences between the financial
reporting basis and the tax basis of the assets and liabilities
 and are measured using enacted tax rates and laws that will be
in effect when the differences are expected to reverse. An allowance against deferred tax assets is recognized when it is more
likely than not that such tax benefits will not be realized.


uncertain tax position only after considering the probability that a tax authority would sustain the position in an
examination. For tax positions meeting a &ldquo;more-likely-than-not&rdquo; threshold
 the amount recognized in the
consolidated financial statements is the benefit expected to be realized upon settlement with the tax authority. For tax
positions not meeting the threshold
 no financial statement benefit is recognized. The Company recognizes interest and
penalties
 if any
 related to uncertain tax positions as a component of other expense. The Company did not have any
unrecognized tax benefits as of May 31
 2017
 and does not expect this to change significantly over the next 12 months.

On February 25
 2016
 the
Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) issued ASU 2016-2
 &#34;Leases&#34; (Topic 842)
 which is intended to improve financial
reporting for lease transactions. This ASU will require organizations that lease assets
 such as real estate and manufacturing
equipment
 to recognize assets and liabilities on their balance sheets for the rights to use those assets for the lease term and
obligations to make lease payments created by those leases that have terms of greater than 12 months. The recognition
 measurement
and presentation of expenses and cash flows arising from a lease by a lessee primarily will depend on its classification as a finance
or operating lease. This ASU will also require disclosures to help investors and other financial statement users better understand
the amount and timing of cash flows arising from leases. These disclosures will include qualitative and quantitative requirements
providing additional information about the amounts recorded in the financial statements. This ASU will be effective for public
entities beginning the first quarter 2019. We do not believe that this ASU will have a material impact on our financial statements.


In November 2015
 the FASB
issued ASU 2015-17
 &#34;Income Taxes
 Balance Sheet Classifications of Deferred Taxes.&#34; This amendment simplifies the presentation
of deferred taxes by requiring that all deferred tax liabilities and assets now be recorded as noncurrent. This amendment is effective


early adoption permissible. The Company will adopt this amendment in 2017. This amendment has no material impact on the Company's
results of operation.


 the FASB issued ASU 2015-14
 &#34;Revenue from Contracts with Customers.&#34;

 2017


 the FASB issued ASU 2015-11
 &#34;Inventory. Simplifying the Measurement of
Inventory.&#34; This amendment only applies to entities that use the first-in
 first-out (FIFO) or average cost methods of valuing
inventory. Entities would measure inventory at the lower of cost and net realizable value. This amendment aligns measurement of
inventory in GAAP with the International Financial Reporting Standards (IFRS). This amendment is effective for annual periods


adopt this amendment in 2017. This amendment has no material impact on the Company's results of operation.

In April 2015
 the FASB
issued ASU 2015-03&nbsp;
 &ldquo;Interest -Imputation of Interest. &ldquo; This guidance requires debt issuance costs
be presented in the balance sheet as a reduction in liability rather than as an asset. This amendment is effective for
interim and reporting periods beginning after December 15
 2016 with early adoption permissible. The Company has elected
early adoption.

On May 14
 2014
 FASB and The International Accounting Standards Board (the &#147;IASB&#148;)
issued a new joint revenue recognition standard that supersedes nearly all GAAP guidance on revenue recognition. The core principal
of the standard is that revenue recognition should depict the transfer of goods and services to customers in an amount that reflects
the consideration to which the entity expects to be entitled in exchange for those goods and services. The new standard is effective

are not known at this time.

 the Company

 $0.001 par value per shares of the Company (the &ldquo;Lender Conversion

 as per the following conversion formula: The number of Lender Conversion Shares equals the amount being converted

 however

000.00 at any time

of any applicable date of conversion.






    
    





 a conversion factor of 70% shall
apply to the Lender Conversion Price
 subject to the following adjustments: (i) if at any me the average of the three (3) lowest
closing bid prices in the twenty (20) trading days immediately preceding any date of measurement is below $1.00
 then in such event
the then-current conversion factor shall be reduced by 10% for all future conversions; (ii) if at any time after the effective

 for all future conversions; and

 as defined
 if any major default occurs
as defined

 $0.001 par value per shares of the Company (the &amp;#147;Lender Conversion Shares&amp;#148;)
&#13;as per the following conversion formula:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 7pt/normal Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt/normal Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;The number of Lender Conversion Shares equals the amount&#13;being converted (the &amp;#34;Conversion Amount&amp;#34;) divided by the Lender Conversion Price.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 7pt/normal Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt/normal Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;The Lender Conversion Price is defined in the Note as being&#13;$3.00 per share
 however
 in the event the Market Capitalization falls below $20
000
000.00 at any time
 then in such event (a)&#13;the Lender Conversion Price for all Lender Conversions occurring after the first date of such occurrence shall equal the lower&#13;of the Lender Conversion Price and the Market Price as of any applicable date of Conversion.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 7pt/normal Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;Subject to certain conditions
 a Conversion Factor of 70%
&#13;shall apply to the Lender Conversion Price
 subject to the following adjustments: (i) If at any time the average of the three&#13;(3) lowest Closing Bid Prices in the twenty (20) Trading Days immediately preceding any date of measurement is below $1.00
&#13;then in such event the then-current Conversion Factor shall be reduced by 10% for all future conversions; (ii) if at any time&#13;after the effective date of the Note
 the Conversion Shares are not DTC Eligible
 then the then-current Conversion Factor&#13;will automatically be reduced by 5% for all future conversions; and
 (iii) in addition to the Default Effect
 as defined
 if&#13;any Major Default occurs
 as defined
 after the effective date of the Note

    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    

    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    


    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    

    
    
    
    
    

    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    

    

    

    
    


    

    
    

    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    

    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    

    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    


    

    
    
    
    
    

    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    

    

    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    

    
    

    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    

    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    


    
    
    
    
    
    

 Inc. (&amp;#8220;HISP&amp;#8221;) and its wholly owned&#13;subsidiary
 Energy Source Distributors Inc.
 (&amp;#8220;ESD&amp;#8221;) for 2017 and only HISP for 2016 (collectively 
 the&#13;&amp;#8220;Company&amp;#8220;). All intercompany balances and transactions have been eliminated in consolidation.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;HISP was incorporated in Delaware in April 2013 and acquired&#13;ESD during July 2016. The Company currently markets and sells traditional Hispanic and other beverages in New York and California.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;br /&gt;&#13;The accompanying consolidated financial statements&#13;have been prepared in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America (&amp;#34;GAAP&amp;#34;).&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Revenue Recognition&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;In general
 the Company records revenue when persuasive evidence&#13;of an arrangement exists
 services have been rendered or product delivery has occurred
 the sales price to the customer is fixed&#13;or determinable
 and collectability is reasonably assured. Provision for sales returns is estimated based&#13;on the Company's historical return experience. Revenue is presented net of returns.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;In March 2017
 the Company discontinued an exclusive distribution&#13;agreement with a vendor. In accordance with the distribution agreement
 the Company received a &amp;#8220;Termination Payment&amp;#8221;
&#13;as define in the amount of $97
731
 which was recorded as other income during the year ended May 31
 2017.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Use of Estimates&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;The preparation of consolidated financial statements in conformity&#13;with GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and&#13;disclosures of contingent assets and liabilities at the dates of the consolidated balance sheets and the reported amounts of revenues&#13;and expenses during the reporting periods. Actual results could differ from those estimates.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Net Loss Per Common Share&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;Basic loss per share is calculated by dividing net loss by the&#13;weighted average number of common shares outstanding for the period. Diluted loss per share is calculated by dividing net loss&#13;by the weighted average number of common shares and dilutive common stock equivalents outstanding. During periods in which the&#13;Company incurs losses
 common stock equivalents
 if any
 are not considered
 as their effect would be anti -dilutive. As of May&#13;31
 2017
 warrants
 related to the convertible notes payable could be converted into approximately 730
000 shares of common stock
&#13;were outstanding.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;The Company utilizes the accrual method of accounting for income&#13;taxes. Under the accrual method
 deferred tax assets and liabilities are determined based on the differences between the financial&#13;reporting basis and the tax basis of the assets and liabilities
 and are measured using enacted tax rates and laws that will be&#13;in effect when the differences are expected to reverse. An allowance against deferred tax assets is recognized when it is more&#13;likely than not that such tax benefits will not be realized.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;The Company recognizes the financial statement benefit of an&#13;uncertain tax position only after considering the probability that a tax authority would sustain the position in an&#13;examination. For tax positions meeting a &amp;#8220;more-likely-than-not&amp;#8221; threshold
 the amount recognized in the&#13;consolidated financial statements is the benefit expected to be realized upon settlement with the tax authority. For tax&#13;positions not meeting the threshold
 no financial statement benefit is recognized. The Company recognizes interest and&#13;penalties
 if any
 related to uncertain tax positions as a component of other expense. The Company did not have any&#13;unrecognized tax benefits as of May 31
 2017
 and does not expect this to change significantly over the next 12 months.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Stock-Based Compensation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;The Company accounts for equity instruments issued to employees&#13;in accordance with ASC 718
 Compensation - Stock Compensation. ASC 718 requires all share-based compensation payments to be recognized&#13;in the financial statements based on the fair value on the issuance date.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;Equity instruments granted to non-employees are accounted for in&#13;accordance with ASC 505
 Equity. The final measurement date for the fair value of equity instruments with performance criteria&#13;is the date that each performance commitment for such equity instrument is satisfied or there is a significant disincentive for&#13;non-performance.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cash and Cash Equivalents&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;The Company considers all highly liquid investments with an original&#13;maturity of three months or less to be cash equivalents.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Accounts Receivable&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;The Company extends credit to its customers in the normal course&#13;of business and performs ongoing credit evaluations of its customers
 maintaining an allowance for potential credit losses. Uncollectible&#13;accounts are written off at the time they are deemed uncollectible.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;Accounts receivable is reported net of an allowance for doubtful&#13;accounts
 when determined necessary. The allowance is based on management's estimate of the amount of receivables that will actually&#13;be collected. As of May 31
 2017 and May 31
 2016
 an allowance for doubtful accounts was not necessary.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Inventory&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;Inventory consists of finished goods and is stated at the lower&#13;of cost (first-in
 first-out) or market value.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Fair Value of Financial Instruments&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt/106% Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0 0 8pt&gt;Pursuant to&amp;#160;ASC No. 820. &amp;#34;Fair Value Measurement&#13;and Disclosures
&amp;#34; the Company is required to estimate the fair value of all financial instruments included on its balance&#13;sheets. The Company considers the carrying value of such amounts in the financial statements to approximate their fair value due&#13;to the short-term nature of these financial instruments.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Advertising&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;Advertising and promotion costs are expensed as incurred. Advertising&#13;and promotion expense amounted to approximately $23
800 and $5
000 for the years ended May 31
 2017 and 2016
 respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Shipping and Handling&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;Shipping and handling costs are included in costs of goods sold.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Recent Pronouncements&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;On February 25
 2016
 the&#13;Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) issued ASU 2016-2
 &amp;#34;Leases&amp;#34; (Topic 842)
 which is intended to improve financial&#13;reporting for lease transactions. This ASU will require organizations that lease assets
 such as real estate and manufacturing&#13;equipment
 to recognize assets and liabilities on their balance sheets for the rights to use those assets for the lease term and&#13;obligations to make lease payments created by those leases that have terms of greater than 12 months. The recognition
 measurement
&#13;and presentation of expenses and cash flows arising from a lease by a lessee primarily will depend on its classification as a finance&#13;or operating lease. This ASU will also require disclosures to help investors and other financial statement users better understand&#13;the amount and timing of cash flows arising from leases. These disclosures will include qualitative and quantitative requirements
&#13;providing additional information about the amounts recorded in the financial statements. This ASU will be effective for public&#13;entities beginning the first quarter 2019. We do not believe that this ASU will have a material impact on our financial statements.&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;In November 2015
 the FASB&#13;issued ASU 2015-17
 &amp;#34;Income Taxes
 Balance Sheet Classifications of Deferred Taxes.&amp;#34; This amendment simplifies the presentation&#13;of deferred taxes by requiring that all deferred tax liabilities and assets now be recorded as noncurrent. This amendment is effective&#13;for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after&lt;font style=color: #222222&gt;&amp;#160;December 15
 2016&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;with&#13;early adoption permissible. The Company will adopt this amendment in 2017. This amendment has no material impact on the Company's&#13;results of operation.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&lt;br /&gt;&#13;In&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt; August 2015
 the FASB issued ASU 2015-14
 &amp;#34;Revenue from Contracts with Customers.&amp;#34;&#13;This amendment defers the effective date of implementation to after&lt;font style=color: #222222&gt;&amp;#160;December 15
 2017&lt;/font&gt;.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;In July 2015
 the FASB issued ASU 2015-11
 &amp;#34;Inventory. Simplifying the Measurement of&#13;Inventory.&amp;#34; This amendment only applies to entities that use the first-in
 first-out (FIFO) or average cost methods of valuing&#13;inventory. Entities would measure inventory at the lower of cost and net realizable value. This amendment aligns measurement of&#13;inventory in GAAP with the International Financial Reporting Standards (IFRS). This amendment is effective for annual periods&#13;beginning after&lt;font style=color: #222222&gt;&amp;#160;December 15
 2016&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;with early adoption permitted. The Company will&#13;adopt this amendment in 2017. This amendment has no material impact on the Company's results of operation.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;In April 2015
 the FASB&#13;issued ASU 2015-03&amp;#160;
 &amp;#8220;Interest -Imputation of Interest. &amp;#8220; This guidance requires debt issuance costs&#13;be presented in the balance sheet as a reduction in liability rather than as an asset. This amendment is effective for&#13;interim and reporting periods beginning after December 15
 2016 with early adoption permissible. The Company has elected&#13;early adoption.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;On May 14
 2014
 FASB and The International Accounting Standards Board (the &amp;#147;IASB&amp;#148;)&#13;issued a new joint revenue recognition standard that supersedes nearly all GAAP guidance on revenue recognition. The core principal&#13;of the standard is that revenue recognition should depict the transfer of goods and services to customers in an amount that reflects&#13;the consideration to which the entity expects to be entitled in exchange for those goods and services. The new standard is effective&#13;for the Company for the fiscal year 2017&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;and the effects of the standard on the Company's consolidated financial statements&#13;are not known at this time.&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;Management does not believe&#13;that any other recently issued
 but not yet effective
 accounting pronouncement
 if adopted


 balances may be in excess of the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation (&amp;#8220;FDIC&amp;#8221;) insurance limit. Cash in&#13;banks is insured by the FDIC up to $250
000 per institution
 per entity. The Company routinely assesses the financial strength&#13;of its customers and
 as a consequence
 believes that its trade account receivable credit risk exposure is limited.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Sales and Accounts Receivable&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;During the year ended May 31

 deferred tax assets and liabilities are determined based on the differences between the financial&#13;reporting basis and the tax basis of the assets and liabilities
 and are measured using enacted tax rates and laws that will be&#13;in effect when the differences are expected to reverse. An allowance against deferred tax assets is recognized when it is more&#13;likely than not that such tax benefits will not be realized.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;The Company recognizes the financial statement benefit of an&#13;uncertain tax position only after considering the probability that a tax authority would sustain the position in an&#13;examination. For tax positions meeting a &amp;#8220;more-likely-than-not&amp;#8221; threshold
 the amount recognized in the&#13;consolidated financial statements is the benefit expected to be realized upon settlement with the tax authority. For tax&#13;positions not meeting the threshold
 no financial statement benefit is recognized. The Company recognizes interest and&#13;penalties
 if any
 related to uncertain tax positions as a component of other expense. The Company did not have any&#13;unrecognized tax benefits as of May 31
 2017

 2016
 the&#13;Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) issued ASU 2016-2
 &amp;#34;Leases&amp;#34; (Topic 842)
 which is intended to improve financial&#13;reporting for lease transactions. This ASU will require organizations that lease assets
 such as real estate and manufacturing&#13;equipment
 to recognize assets and liabilities on their balance sheets for the rights to use those assets for the lease term and&#13;obligations to make lease payments created by those leases that have terms of greater than 12 months. The recognition
 measurement
&#13;and presentation of expenses and cash flows arising from a lease by a lessee primarily will depend on its classification as a finance&#13;or operating lease. This ASU will also require disclosures to help investors and other financial statement users better understand&#13;the amount and timing of cash flows arising from leases. These disclosures will include qualitative and quantitative requirements
&#13;providing additional information about the amounts recorded in the financial statements. This ASU will be effective for public&#13;entities beginning the first quarter 2019. We do not believe that this ASU will have a material impact on our financial statements.&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;In November 2015
 the FASB&#13;issued ASU 2015-17
 &amp;#34;Income Taxes
 Balance Sheet Classifications of Deferred Taxes.&amp;#34; This amendment simplifies the presentation&#13;of deferred taxes by requiring that all deferred tax liabilities and assets now be recorded as noncurrent. This amendment is effective&#13;for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after&lt;font style=color: #222222&gt;&amp;#160;December 15
 2016&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;with&#13;early adoption permissible. The Company will adopt this amendment in 2017. This amendment has no material impact on the Company's&#13;results of operation.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&lt;br /&gt;&#13;In&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt; August 2015
 the FASB issued ASU 2015-14
 &amp;#34;Revenue from Contracts with Customers.&amp;#34;&#13;This amendment defers the effective date of implementation to after&lt;font style=color: #222222&gt;&amp;#160;December 15
 2017&lt;/font&gt;.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;In July 2015
 the FASB issued ASU 2015-11
 &amp;#34;Inventory. Simplifying the Measurement of&#13;Inventory.&amp;#34; This amendment only applies to entities that use the first-in
 first-out (FIFO) or average cost methods of valuing&#13;inventory. Entities would measure inventory at the lower of cost and net realizable value. This amendment aligns measurement of&#13;inventory in GAAP with the International Financial Reporting Standards (IFRS). This amendment is effective for annual periods&#13;beginning after&lt;font style=color: #222222&gt;&amp;#160;December 15
 2016&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;with early adoption permitted. The Company will&#13;adopt this amendment in 2017. This amendment has no material impact on the Company's results of operation.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;In April 2015
 the FASB&#13;issued ASU 2015-03&amp;#160;
 &amp;#8220;Interest -Imputation of Interest. &amp;#8220; This guidance requires debt issuance costs&#13;be presented in the balance sheet as a reduction in liability rather than as an asset. This amendment is effective for&#13;interim and reporting periods beginning after December 15
 2016 with early adoption permissible. The Company has elected&#13;early adoption.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;On May 14
 2014
 FASB and The International Accounting Standards Board (the &amp;#147;IASB&amp;#148;)&#13;issued a new joint revenue recognition standard that supersedes nearly all GAAP guidance on revenue recognition. The core principal&#13;of the standard is that revenue recognition should depict the transfer of goods and services to customers in an amount that reflects&#13;the consideration to which the entity expects to be entitled in exchange for those goods and services. The new standard is effective&#13;for the Company for the fiscal year 2017&amp;#160;&lt;/font&gt;and the effects of the standard on the Company's consolidated financial statements&#13;are not known at this time.&lt;br /&gt;&#13;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 11pt Calibri, Helvetica, Sans-Serif; margin: 0&gt;&lt;font style=background-color: white&gt;Management does not believe&#13;that any other recently issued
 but not yet effective
 accounting pronouncement

Amount due from customers or clients
 within one year of the balance sheet date (or the normal operating cycle
 whichever is longer)
 for goods or services (including trade receivables) that have been delivered or sold in the normal course of business
 reduced to the estimated net realizable fair value by an allowance established by the entity of the amount it deems uncertain of collection.




























Excess of issue price over par or stated value of the entity's capital stock and amounts received from other transactions involving the entity's stock or stockholders. Includes adjustments to additional paid in capital. Some examples of such adjustments include recording the issuance of debt with a beneficial conversion feature and certain tax consequences of equity instruments awarded to employees. Use this element for the aggregate amount of additional paid-in capital associated with common and preferred stock. For additional paid-in capital associated with only common stock
 use the element additional paid in capital
 common stock. For additional paid-in capital associated with only preferred stock
 use the element additional paid in capital
 preferred stock.

























































Sum of the carrying amounts as of the balance sheet date of all assets that are expected to be realized in cash
 sold
 or consumed within one year (or the normal operating cycle
 if longer). Assets are probable future economic benefits obtained or controlled by an entity as a result of past transactions or events.
























































Amount of currency on hand as well as demand deposits with banks or financial institutions. Includes other kinds of accounts that have the general characteristics of demand deposits. Also includes short-term
 highly liquid investments that are both readily convertible to known amounts of cash and so near their maturity that they present insignificant risk of changes in value because of changes in interest rates. Excludes cash and cash equivalents within disposal group and discontinued operation.




























Aggregate par or stated value of issued nonredeemable common stock (or common stock redeemable solely at the option of the issuer). This item includes treasury stock repurchased by the entity. Note: elements for number of nonredeemable common shares
 par value and other disclosure concepts are in another section within stockholders' equity.




























The portion of the carrying value of long-term convertible debt as of the balance sheet date that is scheduled to be repaid within one year or in the normal operating cycle if longer. Convertible debt is a financial instrument which can be exchanged for a specified amount of another security
 typically the entity's common stock
 at the option of the issuer or the holder.




























Including the current and noncurrent portions
 carrying value as of the balance sheet date of a written promise to pay a note
 initially due after one year or beyond the operating cycle if longer
 which can be exchanged for a specified amount of one or more securities (typically common stock)
 at the option of the issuer or the holder.




























The carrying amount of consideration received or receivable as of the balance sheet date on potential earnings that were not recognized as revenue in conformity with GAAP
 and which are expected to be recognized as such within one year or the normal operating cycle
 if longer
 including sales
 license fees
 and royalties
 but excluding interest income.




























Carrying value of amounts transferred to third parties for security purposes that are expected to be returned or applied towards payment after one year or beyond the operating cycle
 if longer.




























Carrying amount as of the balance sheet date of obligations due all related parties. For classified balance sheets
 represents the current portion of such liabilities (due within one year or within the normal operating cycle if longer).

 excluding goodwill

 net of accumulated amortization and impairment charges.

(b))

 or consumed within one year or operating cycle
 if longer.





















































































Amount of liabilities and equity items
 including the portion of equity attributable to noncontrolling interests
 if any.




























Total obligations incurred as part of normal operations that are expected to be paid during the following twelve months or within one business cycle
 if longer.




























The carrying value as of the balance sheet date of the current portion of long-term obligations drawn from a line of credit
 which is a bank's commitment to make loans up to a specific amount. Examples of items that might be included in the application of this element may consist of letters of credit
 standby letters of credit
 and revolving credit arrangements
 under which borrowings can be made up to a maximum amount as of any point in time conditional on satisfaction of specified terms before
 as of and after the date of drawdowns on the line. Includes short-term obligations that would normally be classified as current liabilities but for which (a) postbalance sheet date issuance of a long term obligation to refinance the short term obligation on a long term basis
 or (b) the enterprise has entered into a financing agreement that clearly permits the enterprise to refinance the short-term obligation on a long term basis and the following conditions are met (1) the agreement does not expire within 1 year and is not cancelable by the lender except for violation of an objectively determinable provision
 (2) no violation exists at the BS date
 and (3) the lender has entered into the financing agreement is expected to be financially capable of honoring the agreement.

 par value and other disclosure concepts are in another section within stockholders' equity.




























Amount of asset related to consideration paid in advance for costs that provide economic benefits in future periods

Amount of increase (decrease) in cash and cash equivalents. Cash and cash equivalents are the amount of currency on hand as well as demand deposits with banks or financial institutions. Includes other kinds of accounts that have the general characteristics of demand deposits. Also includes short-term
 highly liquid investments that are both readily convertible to known amounts of cash and so near their maturity that they present insignificant risk of changes in value because of changes in interest rates. Includes effect from exchange rate changes.

taxes. Under the accrual method
 deferred tax assets and liabilities are determined based on the differences between the financial
reporting basis and the tax basis of the assets and liabilities
 and are measured using enacted tax rates and laws that will be
in effect when the differences are expected to reverse. An allowance against deferred tax assets is recognized when it is more
likely than not that such tax benefits will not be realized.


uncertain tax position only after considering the probability that a tax authority would sustain the position in an
examination. For tax positions meeting a &#8220;more-likely-than-not&#8221; threshold
 the amount recognized in the
consolidated financial statements is the benefit expected to be realized upon settlement with the tax authority. For tax
positions not meeting the threshold
 no financial statement benefit is recognized. The Company recognizes interest and
penalties
 if any
 related to uncertain tax positions as a component of other expense. The Company did not have any
unrecognized tax benefits as of May 31

On February 25
 2016
 the
Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) issued ASU 2016-2
 &#34;Leases&#34; (Topic 842)
 which is intended to improve financial
reporting for lease transactions. This ASU will require organizations that lease assets
 such as real estate and manufacturing
equipment
 to recognize assets and liabilities on their balance sheets for the rights to use those assets for the lease term and
obligations to make lease payments created by those leases that have terms of greater than 12 months. The recognition
 measurement
and presentation of expenses and cash flows arising from a lease by a lessee primarily will depend on its classification as a finance
or operating lease. This ASU will also require disclosures to help investors and other financial statement users better understand
the amount and timing of cash flows arising from leases. These disclosures will include qualitative and quantitative requirements
providing additional information about the amounts recorded in the financial statements. This ASU will be effective for public



In November 2015
 the FASB
issued ASU 2015-17
 &#34;Income Taxes
 Balance Sheet Classifications of Deferred Taxes.&#34; This amendment simplifies the presentation
of deferred taxes by requiring that all deferred tax liabilities and assets now be recorded as noncurrent. This amendment is effective


early adoption permissible. The Company will adopt this amendment in 2017. This amendment has no material impact on the Company's
results of operation.


 the FASB issued ASU 2015-14
 &#34;Revenue from Contracts with Customers.&#34;

 2017


 the FASB issued ASU 2015-11
 &#34;Inventory. Simplifying the Measurement of
Inventory.&#34; This amendment only applies to entities that use the first-in
 first-out (FIFO) or average cost methods of valuing
inventory. Entities would measure inventory at the lower of cost and net realizable value. This amendment aligns measurement of
inventory in GAAP with the International Financial Reporting Standards (IFRS). This amendment is effective for annual periods


adopt this amendment in 2017. This amendment has no material impact on the Company's results of operation.

In April 2015
 the FASB
issued ASU 2015-03&#160;
 &#8220;Interest -Imputation of Interest. &#8220; This guidance requires debt issuance costs
be presented in the balance sheet as a reduction in liability rather than as an asset. This amendment is effective for
interim and reporting periods beginning after December 15
 2016 with early adoption permissible. The Company has elected
early adoption.

On May 14
 2014
 FASB and The International Accounting Standards Board (the &#147;IASB&#148;)
issued a new joint revenue recognition standard that supersedes nearly all GAAP guidance on revenue recognition. The core principal
of the standard is that revenue recognition should depict the transfer of goods and services to customers in an amount that reflects
the consideration to which the entity expects to be entitled in exchange for those goods and services. The new standard is effective


&#160;

that any other recently issued
 but not yet effective
 accounting pronouncement
 if adopted
 would have a material effect on the
accompanying consolidated financial statements.

taxes. Under the accrual method

On February 25
 2016
 the
Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) issued ASU 2016-2
 &#34;Leases&#34; (Topic 842)
 which is intended to improve financial
reporting for lease transactions. This ASU will require organizations that lease assets
 such as real estate and manufacturing
equipment
 to recognize assets and liabilities on their balance sheets for the rights to use those assets for the lease term and
obligations to make lease payments created by those leases that have terms of greater than 12 months. The recognition
 measurement
and presentation of expenses and cash flows arising from a lease by a lessee primarily will depend on its classification as a finance
or operating lease. This ASU will also require disclosures to help investors and other financial statement users better understand
the amount and timing of cash flows arising from leases. These disclosures will include qualitative and quantitative requirements
providing additional information about the amounts recorded in the financial statements. This ASU will be effective for public



In November 2015
 the FASB
issued ASU 2015-17
 &#34;Income Taxes
 Balance Sheet Classifications of Deferred Taxes.&#34; This amendment simplifies the presentation
of deferred taxes by requiring that all deferred tax liabilities and assets now be recorded as noncurrent. This amendment is effective


early adoption permissible. The Company will adopt this amendment in 2017. This amendment has no material impact on the Company's
results of operation.


 the FASB issued ASU 2015-14
 &#34;Revenue from Contracts with Customers.&#34;

 2017


 the FASB issued ASU 2015-11
 &#34;Inventory. Simplifying the Measurement of
Inventory.&#34; This amendment only applies to entities that use the first-in
 first-out (FIFO) or average cost methods of valuing
inventory. Entities would measure inventory at the lower of cost and net realizable value. This amendment aligns measurement of
inventory in GAAP with the International Financial Reporting Standards (IFRS). This amendment is effective for annual periods


adopt this amendment in 2017. This amendment has no material impact on the Company's results of operation.

In April 2015
 the FASB
issued ASU 2015-03&#160;
 &#8220;Interest -Imputation of Interest. &#8220; This guidance requires debt issuance costs
be presented in the balance sheet as a reduction in liability rather than as an asset. This amendment is effective for
interim and reporting periods beginning after December 15
 2016 with early adoption permissible. The Company has elected
early adoption.

On May 14
 2014
 FASB and The International Accounting Standards Board (the &#147;IASB&#148;)
issued a new joint revenue recognition standard that supersedes nearly all GAAP guidance on revenue recognition. The core principal
of the standard is that revenue recognition should depict the transfer of goods and services to customers in an amount that reflects
the consideration to which the entity expects to be entitled in exchange for those goods and services. The new standard is effective

Disclosure of accounting policy for advertising costs. For those costs that cannot be capitalized
 discloses whether such costs are expensed as incurred or the first period in which the advertising takes place. For direct response advertising costs that are capitalized

 the types of costs capitalized and the related amortization period. An entity also may disclose its accounting policy for cooperative advertising arrangements.




























Disclosure of accounting policy for cash and cash equivalents
 including the policy for determining which items are treated as cash equivalents. Other information that may be disclosed includes (1) the nature of any restrictions on the entity's use of its cash and cash equivalents
 (2) whether the entity's cash and cash equivalents are insured or expose the entity to credit risk
 (3) the classification of any negative balance accounts (overdrafts)
 and (4) the carrying basis of cash equivalents (for example
 at cost) and whether the carrying amount of cash equivalents approximates fair value.

Disclosure of accounting policy for revenue recognition. If the entity has different policies for different types of revenue transactions
 the policy for each material type of transaction is generally disclosed. If a sales transaction has multiple element arrangements (for example
 delivery of multiple products
 services or the rights to use assets) the disclosure may indicate the accounting policy for each unit of accounting as well as how units of accounting are determined and valued. The disclosure may encompass important judgment as to appropriateness of principles related to recognition of revenue. The disclosure also may indicate the entity's treatment of any unearned or deferred revenue that arises from the transaction.

The net amount of stock issued during the period upon the conversion of convertible securities
 net of adjustments (for example
 to additional paid in capital) including the write-off of an equity component recognized to record the convertible debt instrument as two separate components - a debt component and an equity component. This item is meant to disclose the value of shares issued on conversion of convertible securities that were recorded as two separate (debt and equity) components.




























The maximum number of securities classified as temporary equity that are permitted to be issued by an entity's charter and bylaws. Temporary equity is a security with redemption features that are outside the control of the issuer
 is not classified as an asset or liability in conformity with GAAP
 and is not mandatorily redeemable. Includes any type of security that is redeemable at a fixed or determinable price or on a fixed or determinable date or dates
 is redeemable at the option of the holder
 or has conditions for redemption which are not solely within the control of the issuer. If convertible
 the issuer does not control the actions or events necessary to issue the maximum number of shares that could be required to be delivered under the conversion option if the holder exercises the option to convert the stock to another class of equity. If the security is a warrant or a rights issue
 the warrant or rights issue is considered to be temporary equity if the issuer cannot demonstrate that it would be able to deliver upon the exercise of the option by the holder in all cases. Includes stock with put option held by ESOP and stock redeemable by holder only in the event of a change in control of the issuer.

Under the terms of the Note
 the Note holder has the right
until the outstanding balance has been paid in full
 to convert all or any part of the outstanding balance into shares of fully
paid and non-assessable common stock
 $0.001 par value per shares of the Company (the &#147;Lender Conversion Shares&#148;)
as per the following conversion formula:


being converted (the &#34;Conversion Amount&#34;) divided by the Lender Conversion Price.


$3.00 per share
 however
 in the event the Market Capitalization falls below $20
000
000.00 at any time
 then in such event (a)
the Lender Conversion Price for all Lender Conversions occurring after the first date of such occurrence shall equal the lower
of the Lender Conversion Price and the Market Price as of any applicable date of Conversion.


 a Conversion Factor of 70%
shall apply to the Lender Conversion Price
 subject to the following adjustments: (i) If at any time the average of the three
(3) lowest Closing Bid Prices in the twenty (20) Trading Days immediately preceding any date of measurement is below $1.00
then in such event the then-current Conversion Factor shall be reduced by 10% for all future conversions; (ii) if at any time
after the effective date of the Note
 the Conversion Shares are not DTC Eligible
 then the then-current Conversion Factor
will automatically be reduced by 5% for all future conversions; and
 (iii) in addition to the Default Effect
 as defined
 if
any Major Default occurs
 as defined
 after the effective date of the Note
 the Conversion Factor shall automatically be
reduced for all future conversions by an additional 5% for each of the first three (3) Major Defaults that occur.









The Company is obligated to make payments equal to 10% of future
receipts.

The carrying value as of the balance sheet date of the current and noncurrent portions of long-term obligations drawn from a line of credit
 which is a bank's commitment to make loans up to a specific amount. Examples of items that might be included in the application of this element may consist of letters of credit
 standby letters of credit
 and revolving credit arrangements
 under which borrowings can be made up to a maximum amount as of any point in time conditional on satisfaction of specified terms before
 as of and after the date of drawdowns on the line. Includes short-term obligations that would normally be classified as current liabilities but for which (a) postbalance sheet date issuance of a long term obligation to refinance the short term obligation on a long term basis
 or (b) the enterprise has entered into a financing agreement that clearly permits the enterprise to refinance the short-term obligation on a long term basis and the following conditions are met (1) the agreement does not expire within 1 year and is not cancelable by the lender except for violation of an objectively determinable provision
 (2) no violation exists at the BS date
 and (3) the lender has entered into the financing agreement is expected to be financially capable of honoring the agreement.
